  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_0cc2bfdf-0b9e-47bd-a909-9877514b82b7'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText1255736349773559938" style="display:none">Sang Sorenson used to be the invisible girl in class. As a new student to Ashley Waters High School, Sang hopes that her new friends will be the change she’s been craving and will make fitting in a breeze.<br /><br />But Academy students aren’t there to take it easy. The high school is overcrowded and rife with violence. When fights begin, Sang will uncover the true reason the boys traded in their private school life for a public one. <br /><br />This year, Sang will no longer be invisible. This year, Sang is a target.<br /><br />The principal and vice principal are hot to take Sang down, and her own mother is determined to entrap Sang forever in her belief that the safest place to be is in the shadows. Despite this, Nathan, Luke, Kota, North, Silas, Victor, and Gabriel will discover Sang’s unyielding loyalty.<br /><br />And they will sorely need it.<br /><br />The Academy, supremely influential.<br /><br />If you enjoyed Pretty Little Liars by Sara Shepard or the Gallagher Girls series by Ally Carter, you may enjoy this series.</span>

Other than this there is nothing bad about Sang's character.   <span id="freeText3748353060746862078" style="display:none">GOD I FUCKING LOVE THIS SERIES<br /><br />I have some things that I don't think I will ever get over in this book but that didn't happen.<br />Here they are:<br />-<b>Sang</b> --&gt; who in this world or any other for that matter would name their child <b>SANG</b>. Other than this there is nothing bad about Sang's character. I love that she is oblivous to the boys feelings and even Dr G and Mr B's for that matter.<br />-<u>Mr Green and Mr Blackbourne,&gt;--&gt; how are they teachers, <u>they are bloody 19/20 years old</u>, do people just spawn these academy kids everywhere I mean seriously<br />-THE ACADEMY --&gt; WHAT THE HELL IS THIS ?????????? I NEED TO KNOW OR I AM GOING TO KILL SOMEBODY<br /><br />Other than those things I love this series to bits and I also love the characters and can't wait for more<br /><br />5 stars and beyond</u></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17765774129853305873">The Introductions was the bait, First Days was the hook!<br/><br/>Sang & The Academy boys are the modern day version of Snow White & the 7 dwarfs (& let's not forget the 2 hunk of a teachers). At first I was certain that there's a paranormal side to this book (or maybe there still could be?). The Academy boys are each skilful,handsome, full of surprises & have a lot of mystery to them - i just can't help but think what is it about The Academy?! <br/><br/>Then I come to the parts where sweet, innocent Sang turns all</span>
  <span id="freeText17765774129853305873" style="display:none">The Introductions was the bait, First Days was the hook!<br /><br />Sang &amp; The Academy boys are the modern day version of Snow White &amp; the 7 dwarfs (&amp; let's not forget the 2 hunk of a teachers). At first I was certain that there's a paranormal side to this book (or maybe there still could be?). The Academy boys are each skilful,handsome, full of surprises &amp; have a lot of mystery to them - i just can't help but think what is it about The Academy?! <br /><br />Then I come to the parts where sweet, innocent Sang turns all bad-ass ninja-fighting not once, but twice so I'm all "F#@k yeah!!! Hooray heroine girl" ^_^ &amp; the adoration and kindness the guys give her, oh it's all soooo cute! For some reason these books leave me feeling very youthful (well younger than 25 years of age lol!) I just love them!<br /><br />As I said, the first book of this series kept me curious, so then I go and buy the 2nd book &amp; the rest is history! Now I'm at home twiddling my thumbs and waiting (patiently) for the 4th book dear author of this awesome series!!!<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer600706456179007953">THIS IS AN ADDICTIVE BOOK!<br/><br/>Here it is people, I am hooked! I fell in love with Sang and the nine guys in book one and needed a fix right away. C.L. delivered with book two. No way it could it be as good as one, right? WRONG WRONG AND WRONG! It was a wonderful continuation of book one. The best part was when we start to learn more about the mysterious academy itself! Yay!!<br/><br/>This book makes you fall more in love with Sang and what a truly strong and compassionate person she is. Her strength and loyal</span>
  <span id="freeText600706456179007953" style="display:none">THIS IS AN ADDICTIVE BOOK!<br /><br />Here it is people, I am hooked! I fell in love with Sang and the nine guys in book one and needed a fix right away. C.L. delivered with book two. No way it could it be as good as one, right? WRONG WRONG AND WRONG! It was a wonderful continuation of book one. The best part was when we start to learn more about the mysterious academy itself! Yay!!<br /><br />This book makes you fall more in love with Sang and what a truly strong and compassionate person she is. Her strength and loyalty in this book is just amazing. She is starting to come out of her shell a little and it is wonderful to see her bloom! IT IS TRULY BEAUTIFUL!<br /><br />The guys are just a wonderful as in book one. I was swooning and drooling through the whole book. I still cannot pick just one. They are all amazing! all nine beautiful males that make me giddy! There are lots of tender moments between Sang and the boys that make you want to make you melt!<br /><br /><br />What is wonderful about this book is there is more action and adventure! You get caught up in the mystery of the Academy and why the boys are at Sang's school. Also, more is being exposed with the secrets in Sang's own family! This book just sucks you right in and you find yourself lost in Sang's world. <br /><br />I LOVE THIS BOOK! I AM DYING FOR BOOK THREE! I AM WILLING DO ABOUT ANYTHING TO GET IT NOW! YES I AM THAT HOOKED ON THIS SERIES! I MAY BE OBESSING A LITTLE OVER THIS SERIES. NOT GOING TO LIE, I AM OBSESSED WITH THIS SERIES! <br />I NEED BOOK THREE NOW!!!!!!</span>

<div id="review_587389772" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/587389772" />
    <a title="Siv Therese" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17688800-siv-therese"><img alt="Siv Therese" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1366923291p2/17688800.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/587389772?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Siv Therese" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Siv Therese" href="/user/show/17688800-siv-therese">Siv Therese</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17734876-first-days">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">everyone</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer587389772" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9436799933354355610">First of all, thank god book two came out so shortly after I finished book one, or else I would have gone half mad waiting! I've got no patience what so ever for this series!<br/><br/>Just give me more!<br/><br/>That said. Is this book as good as the first book? YES! Is it better? WAY better! Did I even think it was possible to get better? Nope!<br/><br/>The titles are pretty revealing about the "life-span" for each book. As book one were an introduction for all the main and<br/>second characters, and not to mention the environme</span>
  <span id="freeText9436799933354355610" style="display:none">First of all, thank god book two came out so shortly after I finished book one, or else I would have gone half mad waiting! I've got no patience what so ever for this series!<br /><br />Just give me more!<br /><br />That said. Is this book as good as the first book? YES! Is it better? WAY better! Did I even think it was possible to get better? Nope!<br /><br />The titles are pretty revealing about the "life-span" for each book. As book one were an introduction for all the main and<br />second characters, and not to mention the environment, book two is really about the first few days of school.<br /><br />That said - its soooo much more!<br /><br />Have anyone of you ever read Francine Pascals series - Fearless? I read this when I were a bit younger, and although I'm not totally sure at to why the Fearless series keeps popping into my mind reading these fantastic books by C.L. Stone, they still sneak in every now and then. I absolutely adored Francine Pascals amazing writing and stories, even more now when I'm older and can appreciate it more.<br /><br />Hands down - I'm starting to feel like stalking C.L. Stone for more books, and you know what? The Academy for me, is even better than the fearless series!<br /><br />Sang, oh dear Sang, is my top ten favourite female heroine of all time. The love, confusion, her tender heart, compassion, and now revealing temper, and witty humour had me laughing and shouting with her all the way through angst, pain and laughs.<br /><br />Although, this series is by far anything ordinary...! The elusive Academy is just hinted (and well... those hints are most intriguing). We still don't know much about the place or the people, but we're getting there. And the action, and tension at the ordinary school is getting higher and higher. Creepy students, hot guys, marriage proposals, way to "ugh" teachers, and the oh so mmm... delicious Mr. Blackbourne and charming Doctor Green (should I bee fancying the Academy teacher as well? "giggling")<br /><br />Sangs interaction with the boys always seem to break my heart, or make me laugh so loud my poor neighbour must think I'm bordering on crazy, 3:30am in the night.<br /><br />C.L. Stone - I thank you from the bottom of my heart for this book! It's even better than the first! And I'm uhm... "calmly" await book three!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9436799933354355610" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1953961724?book_show_action=true">Jun 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alaina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alaina" href="/user/show/50620706-alaina">Alaina</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50620706-alaina?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50620706-alaina?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50620706-alaina?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50620706-alaina?shelf=july-challenge-2018">july-challenge-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50620706-alaina?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50620706-alaina?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50620706-alaina?shelf=romance">romance</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1953961724" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7858407772904737491"><b>Second time read. First time review.</b><br/><br/>The gang is still here and they are still trying to find ways to hang out with Sang while protecting her. Of course things don't go their way at all. Nope, shit hits the fan numerous times. First there are things at school that the guys don't approve of. Then there's her home life that suck's major dick. Sang needs to be put in a bubble guys. A protective ass bubble.<br/><br/>Of course Sang doesn't say anything to them because she doesn't want to lose her friendship. Sh</span>
  <span id="freeText7858407772904737491" style="display:none"><b>Second time read. First time review.</b><br /><br />The gang is still here and they are still trying to find ways to hang out with Sang while protecting her. Of course things don't go their way at all. Nope, shit hits the fan numerous times. First there are things at school that the guys don't approve of. Then there's her home life that suck's major dick. Sang needs to be put in a bubble guys. A protective ass bubble.<br /><br />Of course Sang doesn't say anything to them because she doesn't want to lose her friendship. She values that more than anything and doesn't want to be a bother. I have no idea how she's going to handle pushing them aside so that she doesn't become more of a target to everyone in school. No matter what, they protect each other and I love their little wolf pack. <br /><br />I'm still waiting for the smutty stuff to happen because it is a reverse harem.. I can try to be patient but this shit is taking forever. JUST KISS SOMEONE ALREADY. Please?<br /><br />This school they all go to sucks. I seriously have no idea how it's still running. The kids there are assholes and then there's that whole stupid tradition of throwing someone off a god damn balcony. Yup, you read that correctly. OFF A DAMN BALCONY. Assume correctly, that she gets thrown off that damn thing while in a huge fight. Again, shit hits the fan.<br /><br />Overall, I really enjoyed this book and I'm still in love with this series. I can't wait to see what the newest book will have for my eyes!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7858407772904737491" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer700193228" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14461186482349183928">Note: This review/note was edited 12/27<br/><br/>Review Tally - based out of 5<br/><br/><b>OVERALL: 5 STARS</b><br/><br/><b>Story/Plot: 5</b> - This is the second book in <b>The Academy</b> series by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6869072.C_L__Stone' title='C.L. Stone' rel='nofollow noopener'>C.L. Stone</a>. I love this series. I find it fast paced and interesting. This volume had me adding this book to my Comedy shelf - I laughed almost every other page. I also added it to my Thriller/Espionage/Mystery shelf - there was more suspense to this story, as well as more intriguing information dropped regarding the mysterious "Academy." <br/><br/><b>Re-read Va</b></span>
  <span id="freeText14461186482349183928" style="display:none">Note: This review/note was edited 12/27<br /><br />Review Tally - based out of 5<br /><br /><b>OVERALL: 5 STARS</b><br /><br /><b>Story/Plot: 5</b> - This is the second book in <b>The Academy</b> series by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6869072.C_L__Stone" title="C.L. Stone" rel="nofollow noopener">C.L. Stone</a>. I love this series. I find it fast paced and interesting. This volume had me adding this book to my Comedy shelf - I laughed almost every other page. I also added it to my Thriller/Espionage/Mystery shelf - there was more suspense to this story, as well as more intriguing information dropped regarding the mysterious "Academy." <br /><br /><b>Re-read Value: 5</b> - Yes. Just got done re-reading it again, lol. <br /><br /><b>Continue Series: 5</b> - Of course! I cannot wait until the newest book comes out. I keep checking goodreads, amazon and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6869072.C_L__Stone" title="C.L. Stone" rel="nofollow noopener">C.L. Stone</a>'s website for updates.<br /><br /><b>Characters: 5</b> - If you already glanced at my review/note from book 1, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17183128.Introductions__The_Academy___1_" title="Introductions (The Academy, #1) by C.L. Stone" rel="nofollow noopener">Introductions</a>, I list a good number of characters who I love. I don't want to drop spoilers, but at the end of this volume, you find out Mr. Blackbourne's first name is Owen - kinda sexy huh?, although he prefers to go by Mr. Blackbourne. You also find out Dr. Green's first name is Sean, which is another hot sexy name. *sigh*<br /><br /><b>Cover: 4</b> - First off, I love the cover I got, which features Victor. I lowered my rating because for some reason, on my Kindle I have the newly released cover for this book. Don't get me wrong, because I think the that cover is great, just I have a soft spot for the first one. I am a little shallow and apologize.<br /><br /><b>Genre Fulfillment: 5</b> - YA, check. Romance, check. School life, check.<br /><br /><b>Personal Involvement: 5</b> - If you didn't know this was going to be a <b>5</b>, you never read what I wrote. Not that I hold it against you, but trust me when I tell you if you haven't read this series yet, my question is <b>WHY NOT?</b><br /><br /></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_611984475" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/611984475" />
    <a title="Karin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2986009-karin"><img alt="Karin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452362296p2/2986009.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/611984475?book_show_action=true">May 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karin" href="/user/show/2986009-karin">Karin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17734876-first-days">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer611984475" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7266001831379547190">Meet Sang Sorenson, a young woman who has led a pretty miserable existence so far. Her father is never around because he is always working, and her mother is mentally and physically ill. Her mother’s paranoid thinking keeps Sang and her sister Marie as virtual prisoners in their house, and punishment for perceived infractions frequently crosses the line into abuse.<br/><br/>But then Sang stumbles into the arms of Kota, a neighborhood boy, and before she knows it, this deeply insecure and socially awkward </span>
  <span id="freeText7266001831379547190" style="display:none">Meet Sang Sorenson, a young woman who has led a pretty miserable existence so far. Her father is never around because he is always working, and her mother is mentally and physically ill. Her mother’s paranoid thinking keeps Sang and her sister Marie as virtual prisoners in their house, and punishment for perceived infractions frequently crosses the line into abuse.<br /><br />But then Sang stumbles into the arms of Kota, a neighborhood boy, and before she knows it, this deeply insecure and socially awkward girl has been adopted by a tight-knit band of seven gorgeous young men who have plenty of secrets. They attend a mysterious school called The Academy, but will be enrolling in Sang’s public high school for the upcoming semester.<br /><br />Book One, Introductions, is a somewhat slow start to the series, but vital, in that it introduces each of the young men one at a time. You get a really complete picture of each of Sang’s new friends as they meet her and take her under their collective wing. You also meet two young (also handsome) teachers from The Academy, who seem to work very closely with the boys.<br /><br />In Book Two, First Days, the boys and Sang begin the new school year at a large and troubled public school. The first week is incredibly harrowing for everyone, as Sang starts to learn what it is that the boys, and The Academy, are all about.<br /><br />By the end of Book Two, it is clear that not only do the boys have some major secrets, but so does Sang, and the book ends leaving you thirsting for more.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7266001831379547190" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15375497277063123188">This series are just getting better and better!. There's a lot more action and mystery in this book and everything happens in the first five days of school!. <br/><br/>We got to know just a little more about what the Academy is and the "purpose" of my new nine boyfriends (I wish) at the public school. I don't think I will ever decide who I like the most but this time North got to made me laugh, I would love to see Mr. Blackbourne playing the violin (swoon), and Luke is so sweet, although I really like eve</span>
  <span id="freeText15375497277063123188" style="display:none">This series are just getting better and better!. There's a lot more action and mystery in this book and everything happens in the first five days of school!. <br /><br />We got to know just a little more about what the Academy is and the "purpose" of my new nine boyfriends (I wish) at the public school. I don't think I will ever decide who I like the most but this time North got to made me laugh, I would love to see Mr. Blackbourne playing the violin (swoon), and Luke is so sweet, although I really like every one of them. I love how Sang and the guys interact with each other, there's a subtle flirtation but above all is their friendship and loyalty. <br /><br />C.L. Stone you are a genius. You've accomplished to keep the readers completely hooked and eager to know more and more about the story. Book 3 can't come soon enough! <u>THANK YOU SO MUCH</u> for the copy, the least I could do was to give you my honest opinion.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2443263544" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer13435411421050389471">Sang's life is never dull. She's got a troubled family life - her mother is abusive and her father neglectful. Thank goodness she's met the boys from the Academy. While what they do for the Academy remains a secret, it is clear that they all care about Sang and want to help protect her whether it be from her own family, the creepy Vice Principal, the Principal up to no good, or the general jerks in the school. <br/><br/>Ok, so I'm actually up to book 8 as I write this review, but I think it gives me a dif</span>
  <span id="freeText13435411421050389471" style="display:none">Sang's life is never dull. She's got a troubled family life - her mother is abusive and her father neglectful. Thank goodness she's met the boys from the Academy. While what they do for the Academy remains a secret, it is clear that they all care about Sang and want to help protect her whether it be from her own family, the creepy Vice Principal, the Principal up to no good, or the general jerks in the school. <br /><br />Ok, so I'm actually up to book 8 as I write this review, but I think it gives me a different perspective to share. When I was reading book 2, I was a little perturbed by the slow pace - I mean here Sang is surrounded by good-looking guys, but no one has made anything resembling a move on her - but now that I am farther along in the series, I can appreciate that SLOW burn and the build-up of anticipation. It's worth it. Plus, I like the stark contrast between how respectfully the Academy boys treat her versus how other boys from school treat her. I think it highlights how a teenage girl can have romance in her life without all the stuff that jerks do at that age.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13435411421050389471" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_681672824" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/681672824" />
    <a title="Jessicah Layfield" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22530147-jessicah-layfield"><img alt="Jessicah Layfield" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1374812006p2/22530147.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/681672824?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessicah Layfield" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessicah Layfield" href="/user/show/22530147-jessicah-layfield">Jessicah Layfield</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17734876-first-days">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22530147-jessicah-layfield?shelf=ya-books">ya-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22530147-jessicah-layfield?shelf=pure-awesomeness">pure-awesomeness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22530147-jessicah-layfield?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22530147-jessicah-layfield?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer681672824" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15132627799049958619">Title: The Academy - First Days<br/>Author: C.L. Stone<br/>Series?: The Academy<br/>Synopsis:<br/>Sang Sorenson used to be the invisible girl in class. As a new student to Ashley Waters High School, Sang hopes that her new friends will be the change she’s been craving and will make fitting in a breeze.<br/>But Academy students aren’t there to take it easy. The high school is overcrowded and rife with violence. When fights begin, Sang will uncover the true reason the boys traded in their private school life for a public </span>
  <span id="freeText15132627799049958619" style="display:none">Title: The Academy - First Days<br />Author: C.L. Stone<br />Series?: The Academy<br />Synopsis:<br />Sang Sorenson used to be the invisible girl in class. As a new student to Ashley Waters High School, Sang hopes that her new friends will be the change she’s been craving and will make fitting in a breeze.<br />But Academy students aren’t there to take it easy. The high school is overcrowded and rife with violence. When fights begin, Sang will uncover the true reason the boys traded in their private school life for a public one. <br /><br />This year, Sang will no longer be invisible. This year, Sang is a target.<br /><br />The principal and vice principal are hot to take Sang down, and her own mother is determined to entrap Sang forever in her belief that the safest place to be is in the shadows. Despite this, Nathan, Luke, Kota, North, Silas, Victor, and Gabriel will discover Sang’s unyielding loyalty.<br /><br />And they will sorely need it.<br /><br />The Academy, supremely influential.<br /> <br />Why I Read This:<br />I was in love with book one of this series and thus looked all over for a copy of book two, which I do not regret having to buy to read. It was only $3 for my Kindle edition, so it's not much, but I think I would've paid more if I had needed to because I was interested in it.<br /> <br />My Thoughts/Review:<br />This sequel to the first book of The Academy series was amazing. I loved it through and through. While it doesn't have my usual likes for supernatural and things like that, I have always loved a good spy book.<br /> <br />This book starts off when Sang Sorenson and the boys are going to go to their first day of school at the new high school. Of course they stood out, they wore better clothes than everyone else, they were new, they were 7 freaking hot guys and one girl who kept to themselves. Them standing out quickly becomes a problem. Fights ensue, people are hurt, and everyone must stand together to stay out of it.<br /> <br />Sang has a problem with staying out of fights when people are beating up on her friends. In turn, she gets hurt. In turn, the guys are pissed, but also glad that she stepped in. She seriously needs training. Bad.<br /> <br />I loved Sang, don't get me wrong. She's probably my favorite heroin ever. I think she's so clueless that it's funny sometimes, but I get why she's clueless. I mean, she's never had friends before. We're going through more of what happened in the first book, except better than ever, and on a bigger scale. Now, Sang has to avoid certain people in school instead of just her mother, though there's a bit of that in there, too. Sang is so brave and loyal, as well as quite clever, though she tends not to realize it. I absolutely loved her character and while there were a few things I would've done differently, I admired her for the things she did. It was pretty awesome.<br /> <br />Kota, North, Silas, Luke, Nathan, Victor and Gabriel were all wonderful in this book! I lived for the moments where they showed up. I'm having trouble with maintaining who my fave is. I think it's still North, but I'm starting to like Kota, Victor, and Gabriel even more. And Luke. And...everyone else. Dang it! I love them all, but I'm still in love with North. :) They're all so amazing!<br /> <br />So, I highly recommend that you go get this book. It's pretty awesome. Go find it and read it.<br /> <br />I can't wait for the next book to come out! The Academy - Friends Vs. Family (Year One, Book Three)! It sounds uber-good! I'm keeping it on my list of books I'm waiting for to come out!<br /> <br />I give this book 5 out of 5 stars.<br /> <br />~Jessicah<br /> <br />You can find this review and more on my blog at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://jessicahhope.blogspot.com/">http://jessicahhope.blogspot.com/</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15132627799049958619" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_711854253" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/711854253" />
    <a title="Lindsey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5302761-lindsey"><img alt="Lindsey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590442791p2/5302761.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/711854253?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lindsey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lindsey" href="/user/show/5302761-lindsey">Lindsey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5302761-lindsey?shelf=favorite">favorite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5302761-lindsey?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5302761-lindsey?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5302761-lindsey?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5302761-lindsey?shelf=kindle-lendable">kindle-lendable</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer711854253" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9179996610399582864">Now that I have caught my breath, I think I can do this review logically. <br/><br/>I go book one for review from netgalley and the ending left me and knots and with needs that drove me to purchase the next two books. I didn't even look at price I just hit 'buy now' and dove right back in. <br/><br/>I kinda don't know where to begin because I read this book so fast and with such frantic need that I have to collect the jumbled emotions that are still simmering below the surface. <br/><br/>Sang--as a character I get it. I know</span>
  <span id="freeText9179996610399582864" style="display:none">Now that I have caught my breath, I think I can do this review logically. <br /><br />I go book one for review from netgalley and the ending left me and knots and with needs that drove me to purchase the next two books. I didn't even look at price I just hit 'buy now' and dove right back in. <br /><br />I kinda don't know where to begin because I read this book so fast and with such frantic need that I have to collect the jumbled emotions that are still simmering below the surface. <br /><br />Sang--as a character I get it. I know why she is the way she is looking in at her entire situation as an adult. I know that she could possibly be changed for years because of what she has dealt with and what life handed her. We still don't totally know what drives her mother. I just can't believe that logically getting 'sick' would turn the mother into a wannabe version of Sybil's mother. She literally wants to hurt Sang, make her suffer, and beat her until she is a void shell of a person. I think considering she is doing very well especially considering the fact how overwhelming her 'boys' are. I call them Sang's because they are. Every single one of them is Sang's. <br /><br />That brings me too:<br /><br />Kota<br />Luke<br />Nathan<br />Gabriel<br />Victor<br />Silas<br />North<br /><br />Or as I like to call them: Sang's Boys<br /><br />Let's face it, all the people doing reviews saying this isn't a romance and there is no romance its 'friendship' is in denial. The author did a great job at writing each individual scene with Sang and the boys and telling the story of their relationship growth without making you vomit. <br /><br />It is intense, it is volatile, and it is in a way healthy for Sang. Each of them collectively make a whole, perfect man. They all have amazing attributes that seem to push Sang closer to a form of recovery. I would like her to have more contact with Mr. Blackbourne and Dr. Green, only because I believe she needs their words and their truths to guide her. The boys are so wrapped up in her ultimate protection and just wanting to be with her that they lose what she really needs--therapy. I'm a bit shocked no one has brought it up to be honest. <br /><br />All I know is when I read these books, I literally feel the book in my system. From my head to the my toes I'm physically and emotionally affected. I want this to work. <br /><br />At this point I'm #TeamSilas #TeamNorth (They are the big strong bad boys that's why lol)</span>
  <a data-text-id="9179996610399582864" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1070448623" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1070448623" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10206920434010408952">I keep asking myself why I'm reading this book.<br/><br/>Is it because of the wonderful prose? No...not really.<br/>Is it because of the diverse and dynamic characters? Nope<br/>Is it because of the plot line? Definitely not.<br/><br/>What it has come down to with me is most likely sheer jealousy. <b>I</b> wanted to have friends like "the guys" in high school. I could have used them since a crazy guy was stalking me at school. I would have fed them and loved them and called them George and let them play on the basketball court in t</span>
  <span id="freeText10206920434010408952" style="display:none">I keep asking myself why I'm reading this book.<br /><br />Is it because of the wonderful prose? No...not really.<br />Is it because of the diverse and dynamic characters? Nope<br />Is it because of the plot line? Definitely not.<br /><br />What it has come down to with me is most likely sheer jealousy. <b>I</b> wanted to have friends like "the guys" in high school. I could have used them since a crazy guy was stalking me at school. I would have fed them and loved them and called them George and let them play on the basketball court in the backyard. I promise I would walk them every day and play fetch with them and groom them and clean up after them. Pleeeeeeassssssse?<br /><br />More than anything, this story is unbelievable and that holds some charm with me. All of the guys get along and it is <i>effing magical</i>. I have never know 9 guys, not even on a team of some sort or in a family to get along so well. It's amazing and not possible at all. It is a little dream world in this book and I appreciate it for that.<br /><br />A few things to pick on that are driving me crazy though (more so than other elements in the book)<br /><br />Sang...learn the freaking violin. Victor spend how much on it so he could play with you and he is an amazing musician and you won't learn it when <i>you are specifically taking a class to do so</i>. Come on.<br /><br />Two...will please one of the guys step up and just kiss her or Sang step up and kiss one of the boys? I don't care if it is on the cheek or whatever but please. That line has to be crossed at some point and there were so many great opportunities for it in this book. <b>I want some conflict.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="10206920434010408952" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer2187923330083481295">I have read some other reviews of the books in this series that liken it to a car crash. You know you shouldn't look but you just can't turn away. This is an accurate comparison. The books aren't literary gold by any means and I found this installment slower moving than the first. The bulk of this book is concentrated on the boys touching or holding hands with or making eyes at Sang while she overanalyzes the "normalcy" of the situation. News flash: no, it's not normal. Then there's Dr. Green, a</span>
  <span id="freeText2187923330083481295" style="display:none">I have read some other reviews of the books in this series that liken it to a car crash. You know you shouldn't look but you just can't turn away. This is an accurate comparison. The books aren't literary gold by any means and I found this installment slower moving than the first. The bulk of this book is concentrated on the boys touching or holding hands with or making eyes at Sang while she overanalyzes the "normalcy" of the situation. News flash: no, it's not normal. Then there's Dr. Green, an Acadamy liaison at the school. Maybe it's just me but I get a creeper vibe from him. I know he's not much older than Sang but still. <br />Just when you think the story is going nowhere.....bam! the action kicks in. Then Stone leaves you with a cliffhanger in the last chapter, revealing a secret about Sang that she herself doesn't know. <br />It seems like I am trash talking this book but in all honesty I will probably read the next book out of sheer morbid curiosity then after I finish it I'll hate myself a little bit. Kinda like watching a bad soap opera. To quote another reviewer " if you haven't read this series run! run while you still can! "</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13844217753140827042">I received a copy of this book in exchange for an honest review.<br/><br/>These books are really fun little YA stories that keep me guessing! I'm still dying to know more about The Academy and all the boys, but this installment gave me a lot of answers to the questions I had. We're still following around Sang, who has really started to grow into her new role with the boys. She's stronger and even stood up for herself pretty nicely in this story.   <span id="freeText13844217753140827042" style="display:none">I received a copy of this book in exchange for an honest review.<br /><br />These books are really fun little YA stories that keep me guessing! I'm still dying to know more about The Academy and all the boys, but this installment gave me a lot of answers to the questions I had. We're still following around Sang, who has really started to grow into her new role with the boys. She's stronger and even stood up for herself pretty nicely in this story. I'm glad she didn't stay in her timid shell this time.<br /><br />I'm eagerly awaiting some YA dreamy romance to begin any minute! All these adorable boys are driving me crazy. I'm hoping that things don't spiral out of control too quickly, but this insane love octagon is starting to worry me. Who do I want Sang to end up with? The choices are endless! So many boys!!<br /><br />In case you can't tell, I'm completely hooked on this series and was completely bummed that I can't just jump right into the next one. These are the perfect books for a light afternoon read.</span>

So the first book is all about introducing the boys. This one gets a little more down to business. The boys there are 7 yes I said 7 from an elite school only known as the Academy.   <span id="freeText7113573386680359741" style="display:none">So I read the first book in this series and it left me so curious I had to read more. Now I have finished book two and I'm addicted. Book three pulezz! So the first book is all about introducing the boys. This one gets a little more down to business. The boys there are 7 yes I said 7 from an elite school only known as the Academy. There cover story is that they are at the local high school to help clean it up. There is bullying, inappropriate behaviors and dress, but these students take it to the extreme. Sang and the boys uncover a hideous ritual and have to try to stop it before it's too late. So all in all again it's a huge build up and I don't think the author disappoints. The storyline though it still doesn't explain a lot it will keep you guessing right up to the end. all in all both books in the series are good quick reads that will keep you turning the page and leave you puzzled. I look forward to the next installment. Just going out on a hunch here but I think we might see some romance between Sang and one of the boys just not quite sure which one. M</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11195908339747303602">Reread 6/27/19<br/><br/>This book gives more insight on the boys. They are still gorgeous. <br/><br/>Now Sang ins't the only one sneaking out. Her is sister Marie is too. Marie is a little annoying but the book doesn't follow her moves very much. A big thank you there.<br/><br/>I still can't decide who I want sang to be with. I want her with one guy but the something happens and I want her to another guy. It's so hard. <br/><br/>Getting the third book soon.</span>

          </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/73309161-searcy?shelf=_borrowed-read">_borrowed-read</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2344473351" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16698092403175941611"><b>Second read:</b><br/><br/>Yep, I am still addicted to this series. Addicted to the sugar rush. Addicted to the interaction between these characters. Addicted even to the slow slow slow dive into the bizarre mystery that is the Academy, and the slow slow slower burn that is the developing relationships.<br/><br/>Nothing is particularly realistic in the entire GHOST BIRD series. We are really supposed to believe most of these characters are 15-16 years old? Mostly just starting sophomore year in high school? But mostly t</span>
  <span id="freeText16698092403175941611" style="display:none"><b>Second read:</b><br /><br />Yep, I am still addicted to this series. Addicted to the sugar rush. Addicted to the interaction between these characters. Addicted even to the slow slow slow dive into the bizarre mystery that is the Academy, and the slow slow slower burn that is the developing relationships.<br /><br />Nothing is particularly realistic in the entire GHOST BIRD series. We are really supposed to believe most of these characters are 15-16 years old? Mostly just starting sophomore year in high school? But mostly trained operatives? And financially independent? Hell...even with driver's licenses and cars?! That the two 19 year olds are working as teachers in high school? That one of the 19 year olds is also a doctor? *cough* Uh... okaaaay.<br /><br />But maybe that is part of the allure of this series. The total, incomprehensible, feel good escapism of it. Maybe one of these days, or one of these reviews, I will figure out what it is about this series that keeps me coming back, despite all its flaws.<br /><br />Because I love it. And I really hate that I do. LOL<br /><br />You know you wanna join me :)<br /><br /><b>Original read:</b><br /><br />With this series, I am not sure the star rating really applies normally. If I look critically at the plot, pacing, character development, main character (the most passive wet noodle in existence that I still somehow root for), and other specifics of this series - then it would probably rank somewhere between 2 &amp; 3 stars for most of the books.<br /><br />But C.L. Stone somehow stirs all these slightly-rotten ingredients together and comes out with a delightfully delicious guilty pleasure. I don't get it, but most of the time I can't stop grinning as I eat (read) it.<br /><br />So instead, my stars reflect my ultimate enjoyment, I guess. Rather than any sort of critical assessment. And I will just ignore how many times I've smacked my head on the desk in disbelief or frustration :)</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_674453316" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/674453316" />
    <a title="Nereid" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7761984-nereid"><img alt="Nereid" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587267054p2/7761984.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/674453316?book_show_action=true">Jul 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nereid" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nereid" href="/user/show/7761984-nereid">Nereid</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17734876-first-days">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer674453316" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1120781597424069029">A good storyteller captivates the reader and keeps them guessing and whilst I did get frustrated at times because of the lack of information surrounding the "The Academy" and its students, I yearned to know more. We meet Sang in book 1 "Introductions" and now we have a complete picture of the group. Initially I did question the validity of seven young gorgeous guys befriending an innocent and naive girl yet the relationship they develop with her is almost sister-like at times with undertones of </span>
  <span id="freeText1120781597424069029" style="display:none">A good storyteller captivates the reader and keeps them guessing and whilst I did get frustrated at times because of the lack of information surrounding the "The Academy" and its students, I yearned to know more. We meet Sang in book 1 "Introductions" and now we have a complete picture of the group. Initially I did question the validity of seven young gorgeous guys befriending an innocent and naive girl yet the relationship they develop with her is almost sister-like at times with undertones of flirtatious banter but never really crossing that fine line into seduction. The boys are a godsend to Sang and a conundrum that she is desperate to unravel but she is frustrated by the lack of information and I totally understand that. Sang's childhood is tragic and Kota and his friends acceptance and offer of friendship warms her heart and instils in her a loyalty to them that won't be denied. We all have this need to belong and high school is stressful enough without the added problems of huge secrets and a hidden agenda that Sang is not privy to. She will do whatever it takes to be their friend, keeping their secrets and standing up for them when it counts the most. She was such a likeable character unlike other whiny YA girls and despite dealing with physical and mental abuse, she never really saw herself as a victim. On the surface this book reads like any typical YA yet it deals with some powerful stuff like bullying and abusive behaviour showing that the power of one can make a huge difference. I am really looking forward to reading the next book in the series, it has now become a new favourite of mine.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1120781597424069029" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('CJevl5oRDiWGWhWMjTByrLVUvk+zK5pd8o8Wrb+dKbrC7ioMkskmp6fHjIShvgNH9IcOIZyTuJ9kzkii1gPXVw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('40Yh4gciDbhXYlql1Qw2oMiWNQh0HqXfIEF5vOokds8pP6R5D/olOnb/w635gkdLiUWFZlumhx22ACezg7qIIg==')})
  }
